## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, a fundamental constitutive relation in solid mechanics and materials science. Temperature affects elastic modulus, yield strength, and strain hardening behavior through thermal softening and thermally-activated deformation mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) (temperature-dependent Hooke's law)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic deformation)
- Temperature-dependent power-law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally-softened hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic combined response)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturation-type strain hardening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (coupled hardening and thermal softening)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T)**c3 (power-law thermal softening)
- Arrhenius flow stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally-activated deformation)
- Polynomial thermoelastic: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic temperature-dependent modulus)
- Ludwik-type with thermal: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (combined elastic-plastic with thermal effect)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart creep law inverted)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * exp(c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Bilinear with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * tanh(c2 * epsilon)) * (c3 + c4 * T) (bilinear hardening with softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent modulus → Multiplicative factor (c0 + c1*T) or exp(c2*T) multiplying strain terms
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or rational epsilon/(epsilon + c) forms
- Power-law creep/plasticity → epsilon**n where n is typically between 0.1 and 0.5 for metals
- Thermal softening near melting → (Tm - T)**c form where stress vanishes at critical temperature
- Thermally-activated flow → Arrhenius factor exp(c/T) coupling with strain terms indicates dislocation glide mechanisms
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Sum of linear term (c*epsilon) and nonlinear term (c*epsilon**n) representing distinct deformation regimes
- Strain-temperature coupling → Product form f(epsilon)*g(T) indicates separable thermal and mechanical contributions (Johnson-Cook assumption)
- Concave-up stress-strain at high T → Exponential or sinh strain dependence indicating creep-dominated regime
